[18:21:50] - Custom field `product_accordion_2_product_accordion_body` will be updated with value `<h3>How do you get the flooring underneath the slideout?</h3> To run the flooring underneath a slideout you can do it one of two ways. <strong>Option 1:</strong> Extend the slide fully. Remove any gaskets that run along the bottom of the slide opening. Next, with bottle jacks and a couple of 2x4's, jack up the slide box a few inches to give you space to slide the new flooring in. Finally, install the new flooring, lower the jacks, and put the gasket back on. If your camper has/needs additional wear bars, I recommend this one: <a href="https://store.lci1.com/wear-bar-10ft-117478.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener">https://store.lci1.com/wear-bar-10ft-117478.html</a> <strong>Option 2:</strong> Use a crowbar or hammer to pry up the edge of the subfloor enough that you can slide a block of wood underneath. This way, you have enough room to slide the flooring under the slide subfloor. Go as far back with the flooring as you can without pushing past the exterior seal/wiper. <strong>Important:</strong> When jacking the slide box up or prying on the subfloor, be mindful of the top as there are only a few inches of space between the top and camper opening. <img class="aligncenter size-large wp-image-1854" src="https://cahillscreative.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/IMG_7116-1024x1024.jpg" alt="" width="1024" height="1024" /> <h3>How did you trim the front edge of the slideout?</h3> Since my slideout was angled, I cut strips of the flooring and glued/screwed them to the front edge with 1/4" screws. Then, I used caulk to fill the gap between the main slideout flooring and the front strip. <img class="aligncenter wp-image-1856 size-large" src="https://cahillscreative.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/IMG_7110-1024x1024.jpg" alt="" width="1024" height="1024" /> <p style="text-align: left;">Another method would be to rip a 1"x3" board at a 12.5-degree angle, then attach it to the angled edge with wood glue and 1/2" finish nails. This will make the edge square, and then you can add stair nose trim to give you the finished look.</p> <p style="text-align: center;"><img class="aligncenter wp-image-1857 size-full" src="https://cahillscreative.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/IMG_7108.jpg" alt="" width="828" height="828" /></p> <p style="text-align: center;"><img class="aligncenter wp-image-1858 size-large" src="https://cahillscreative.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/IMG_7106-1024x1024.jpg" alt="" width="1024" height="1024" /></p> <img class="aligncenter wp-image-1855 size-large" src="https://cahillscreative.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/IMG_7113-1024x1024.jpg" alt="" width="1024" height="1024" /> <h3>How do you keep the slideout from scratching the flooring?</h3> My model only had two 12" wear bars on each end of the slideout, so I ran an additional 10' wear bar underneath the entire slideout for an extra lift when retracting in. Also, I definitely recommend getting a set or two of <a href="https://amzn.to/30ryj8v" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Slide-Out Slickers</a> for the corners and center of the slideout. The corners typically cause the most wear so that the slickers will prevent any contact with your flooring.` for post `How to Install Camper Flooring` ...
